<div id="review_203006590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203006590" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203006590?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=will-continue-series">will-continue-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=narration-is-great">narration-is-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=zombie">zombie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=disturbing-gender-comments">disturbing-gender-comments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=audio-also-listened-to">audio-also-listened-to</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=only-listeneed-to">only-listeneed-to</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=listened-to-audio-only">listened-to-audio-only</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203006590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2007531406386520669">I listened to the narration and it was decently narrated, although the narrator sounds very young. But, then again in this story the main character Deuce is really young. Outpost begins when Deuce is 15.5 years old. <br/><br/>So I enjoyed Enclave, the first in this series, but didn’t love it. I was lukewarm enough about that book that I waited months after the release of Enclave to start it. Ultimately, Enclave addressed all of my concerns about Outpost and is such a better book than the first one in this</span>
  <span id="freeText2007531406386520669" style="display:none">I listened to the narration and it was decently narrated, although the narrator sounds very young. But, then again in this story the main character Deuce is really young. Outpost begins when Deuce is 15.5 years old. <br /><br />So I enjoyed Enclave, the first in this series, but didn’t love it. I was lukewarm enough about that book that I waited months after the release of Enclave to start it. Ultimately, Enclave addressed all of my concerns about Outpost and is such a better book than the first one in this series. <br /><br />The beginning of the book starts slow. Almost too slow. The set-up explains how Deuce, Stalker, Fade and Teagan are doing in Salvation. Deuce is not happy, Salvation has strict gender division rules and education rules pertaining to children and these pose problems for Deuce. The gender divisions are irritating, almost to the point of not wanting to read about them. However, the book quickly turns the corner from a slow beginning to action upon action mixing in sweet romance and some pretty good town tension. <br /><br />Ann Aguirre’s books spend a lot of time in the minds of the main character. It seems to <br />be her style of writing and both Sirantha Jax and the Corinne Solomon series are similarly done. There are huge passages with only the heroine’s inner monologue going on and the heroine providing explanations for why other people are feeling certain things and doing certain things. At some points it is irritating, some points it is not believable but usually this is very well done. It is an amazing way to learn about the main character and truly be her. <br /><br />One of the problems I had with Enclave was that there was absolutely no explanation as to why society ended and where the freaks came from. Outpost changes all of that. Looking for an explanation of what caused the devastation? Aguirre provides some history in this book and adds a wonderful twist that completely distinguishes the Enclave series from other zombie and post-apoc books. It is enough to say, that this deviation from the standard storyline of the zombie genre makes reading this book worth it – factor in the emotional development of Deuce and her growing relationships with her friends and this book is a great read. <br /><br />Okay, rape. Ms. Aguirre seems to speak through her characters and attempt to address readers concerns about Stalker and his past actions. Somewhere near the beginning of the story, Deuce has a conversation with Teagan about her abuse at the hand of the Wolves. As I read this section, I felt the author was explaining to the readers and trying to justify Stalker’s presence as an acceptable character despite his past. The reasoning was this – authority taught the followers of a group (The Wolves – Stalker and the Enclave – Deuce) to commit violence in support of the group. The followers of each group (both Stalker and Deuce) bought into these ideas for the betterment of their group. Now that Stalker and Deuce have left these groups they are able to re-evaluate these ideas and their respective roles in the violence they committed. This issue is revisited multiple times throughout the book. At one point Deuce tells Teeagan, “I don’t care if you ever forgive Stalker.” Almost as if Ms. Aguiree is talking to her readers – you don’t need to forgive Stalker or accept that his background made him do it, you can still enjoy the story. I am not sure if I agree with this concept nor do I accept it. However, I appreciate the author’s willingness to address readers’ concerns. Additionally, Ms. Aguirre doesn’t let Teagan just move on past her past attacks. Realistically, the pain and suffering Teagan endured from the gang rape and beatings from the Wolves is not just pushed under a rug – but Teeagan continues to suffer from fear of boys and the need to be safe. <br /><br />Outpost ends with a hell of a cliffhanger. Horribly tense yet hopeful. I cannot wait to read #3 in this series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2007531406386520669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_160015269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160015269" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3594840-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466726414p2/3594840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160015269?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/3594840-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160015269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3299361766446900448">Deuce and her friends may be free from the claustrophobic tunnels of the enclave but life is no less confining for her in Salvation, a town that doesn't appreciate the hunter skills which she has honed and perfected.<br/><br/>Outpost is very much a character driven novel. I find it fascinating watching how Deuce, Fade, Tegan and Stalker develop in a world where adults have manipulated & abandoned them. Now in Salvation the adults try to save a childhood for the four that has long past. These kids have liv</span>
  <span id="freeText3299361766446900448" style="display:none">Deuce and her friends may be free from the claustrophobic tunnels of the enclave but life is no less confining for her in Salvation, a town that doesn't appreciate the hunter skills which she has honed and perfected.<br /><br />Outpost is very much a character driven novel. I find it fascinating watching how Deuce, Fade, Tegan and Stalker develop in a world where adults have manipulated &amp; abandoned them. Now in Salvation the adults try to save a childhood for the four that has long past. These kids have lived through and survived things that the adults will never understand. The residents know of the Freaks but they have a sense of normalcy with schools, enough food to eat and even families. They "breed" for love, a concept that is completely foreign to Deuce.<br /><br />Deuce is one of my all time favorite female characters. She is totally bad ass and knows that the people of Salvation don't understand the severity of the threat from the Freaks. On the other hand she has a bravado that only a teenager can have, thinking they know everything and have seen everything. She's right to an extent, but there is still so much more to learn. The wonderful thing about Deuce is that she's willing to admit when she's wrong, share in the responsibility and ask for help when she needs it. <br /><br />The relationships between the four friends shifts throughout. Salvation is just that - salvation to some but to others it's a false sense of security. The emotions are raw and tender as these children - and yes, I think that's what gets to me the most about this series, is that they are children - try to navigate something as simple as a touch or a kiss while fighting for their lives. <br /><br />I know the tendency is to focus on the romance and you will be richly rewarded on that front, but I'm pleased that Aguirre also pays attention to Tegan and Deuce's relationship. I think we tend to overlook friendships between girlfriends at times and I love the awkwardness and loyalty between these two girls. <br /><br />Now for the real threat. The Freaks. There were a few scenes in the beginning of Outpost that almost…almost…had me sympathizing with them. Or at least maybe humanizing them a tad. But then, holy sh*t! I don't think I've ever been that creeped out before. My heart hurt by the end of Outpost. I was put through an emotional wringer, spit out and sprinkled with a dash of hope.<br /><br />I just can't even fathom what's coming next for my favorite rag tag group of survivors. <br /><br />The name of the final book in the Razorland trilogy is Horde so yeah…..my imagination is working overtime. <br /><br />Disclosure: I was a beta reader for this book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3299361766446900448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_358084774" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358084774" />
    <a title="Kerry *Pale Daughter*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9274536-kerry-pale-daughter"><img alt="Kerry *Pale Daughter*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548639605p2/9274536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358084774?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry *Pale Daughter*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry *Pale Daughter*" href="/user/show/9274536-kerry-pale-daughter">Kerry *Pale Daughter*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9274536-kerry-pale-daughter?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9274536-kerry-pale-daughter?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358084774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4335959734156702336">If you haven't read Enclave and Outpost, you have been missing out on what I consider to be one of the most thought provoking post apocalyptic series around these days. Outpost has everything most dystopian fans love; action, savage rotting zombie-like creatures called Freaks (which are freakin disgusting), and a love story. Yes,I admit that it is my least favorite sort of love story (the dreaded love triangle), yet I feel that the author uses it tactfully as a device to emphasize that Deuce is </span>
  <span id="freeText4335959734156702336" style="display:none">If you haven't read Enclave and Outpost, you have been missing out on what I consider to be one of the most thought provoking post apocalyptic series around these days. Outpost has everything most dystopian fans love; action, savage rotting zombie-like creatures called Freaks (which are freakin disgusting), and a love story. Yes,I admit that it is my least favorite sort of love story (the dreaded love triangle), yet I feel that the author uses it tactfully as a device to emphasize that Deuce is going through some pretty major inner conflict. So that's okay.<br /> <br />All of these exciting features are awesome, and the novel can be enjoyed for these qualities alone. In my opinion, however, it is also the amazing world building and character development in Outpost that makes it so special. Instead of the urban underground, where every day is a brutal battle for survival, Deuce finds herself in a safehaven; a settlement inhabited by, according to the author's notes, the descendents of the Pennsylvania Amish. Talk about trying to fit a square peg into a round hole. No longer considered an adult at the age of 15, Deuce is forced to attend school for the first time, wear a dress (although she craftily wears her Hunter garb beneath) and adapt to Salvation's expectations of how a girl her age should act (ie. learn to sew.) She struggles, and fails, to identify with any role except of that of a deadly huntress, responsible for her society's survival. <br /><br />I love how the author uses love as one of the themes of this novel (and not just the romantic type). In her former society, the elders were young as nobody survived past their 20's. Deuce is totally amazed by the fact that people could actually live to middle-age. She is adopted by an older couple and struggles with the fact that they are actually growing to love her. She has no experience with this emotion (with the exception of a little romantic "sparking" haha) as she has only vague memories of her "dam" and none of her "sire". This is beside the point anyway, since her former society did not encourage such emotion, even among the "breeders". Her growing familial feelings toward her new family and Longshot are a great source of confusion.<br /><br />There are only shades of grey in this novel. Salvation, like College, is imperfect, as are it's inhabitants. Deuce, Fade and Stalker all took turns irritating me. That's one thing that makes Outpost so believable. I'm in love with everything about the book. Except for the Freaks, of course.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4335959734156702336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12868691479052119473">This was a pretty good sequel. It wasn't as exciting as the first book, because they were in the town and not trying to survive everyday. It was interesting seeing Deuce, Fade, Stalker, and Theresa adjust to a regulated life, where women are relegated to housework and serving their husbands and Deuce is considered a child and not valued for her fighting skills. I liked seeing her and Stalker bond and he does seem more trustworthy and dependable. I was somewhat disappointed with Fade, he drew awa</span>
  <span id="freeText12868691479052119473" style="display:none">This was a pretty good sequel. It wasn't as exciting as the first book, because they were in the town and not trying to survive everyday. It was interesting seeing Deuce, Fade, Stalker, and Theresa adjust to a regulated life, where women are relegated to housework and serving their husbands and Deuce is considered a child and not valued for her fighting skills. I liked seeing her and Stalker bond and he does seem more trustworthy and dependable. I was somewhat disappointed with Fade, he drew away from Deuce and couldn't tell her how he felt. I hope their relationship gets better in the next book. The situation with the freaks is getting a lot more interesting and I'm looking forward to how that plays out. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wZdxrt+gDt7AAwA++zwM3wAqw7ha7CLgJrRxmFeEBAQZ4rE+xdie6MpeuxDEjYEkGIVwkIIBdoWOnlISMlV6tA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4f6IXVmW+ISfgl1FtmOU5u9VPlxmGUXhhgJJTlCwxC85i0jNQ+5ospXf5muJ0hkd9/qNdL70EYQuKGrENWG6nw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2819126286835849338">New York Times and USA Today bestselling author Ann Aguirre has been a clown, a clerk, a savior of stray kittens, and a voice actress, not necessarily in that order. She grew up in a yellow house across from a cornfield, but now she lives in Mexico with her family. She writes all kinds of genre fiction, but she has an eternal soft spot for a happily ever after.</span>
